blender_addon.py
```python
'''
Blender add-on for importing, editing, and exporting player models in JSON/DDS format.
'''
import bpy
import json
from bpy_extras.io_utils import ImportHelper, ExportHelper
class BlenderAddon:
    def import_model(self, json_file, dds_file):
        '''
        Imports player model from JSON and DDS files.
        :param json_file: Path to the JSON file containing model data.
        :param dds_file: Path to the DDS file containing texture data.
        '''
        try:
            with open(json_file, 'r') as file:
                model_data = json.load(file)
            # Load DDS texture
            texture = bpy.data.images.load(dds_file)
            # Create mesh and apply texture
            mesh = bpy.data.meshes.new(name="PlayerModel")
            obj = bpy.data.objects.new("PlayerModel", mesh)
            bpy.context.collection.objects.link(obj)
            obj.data.materials.append(bpy.data.materials.new(name="PlayerMaterial"))
            obj.data.materials[0].use_nodes = True
            bsdf = obj.data.materials[0].node_tree.nodes["Principled BSDF"]
            tex_image = obj.data.materials[0].node_tree.nodes.new('ShaderNodeTexImage')
            tex_image.image = texture
            obj.data.materials[0].node_tree.links.new(bsdf.inputs['Base Color'], tex_image.outputs['Color'])
            print(f"Model imported from {json_file} and {dds_file}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error importing model: {e}")
    def edit_model(self):
        '''
        Edits the player model.
        '''
        try:
            # Example: Apply a simple transformation
            for obj in bpy.context.selected_objects:
                obj.scale = (1.1, 1.1, 1.1)
            print("Model edited successfully.")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error editing model: {e}")
    def export_model(self, output_json, output_dds):
        '''
        Exports player model to JSON and DDS files.
        :param output_json: Path to save the JSON file.
        :param output_dds: Path to save the DDS file.
        '''
        try:
            # Export model data to JSON
            model_data = {"example": "model data"}  # Replace with actual model data
            with open(output_json, 'w') as json_file:
                json.dump(model_data, json_file, indent=4)
            # Export texture to DDS
            for obj in bpy.context.selected_objects:
                if obj.type == 'MESH' and obj.data.materials:
                    texture = obj.data.materials[0].node_tree.nodes['ShaderNodeTexImage'].image
                    texture.save_render(output_dds)
            print(f"Model exported to {output_json} and {output_dds}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error exporting model: {e}")
```

asset_reader.py
```python
'''
Module for reading NBA 2k26 assets and exporting them to JSON and DDS formats.
'''
import json
import os
from PIL import Image
import struct
class NBA2K26AssetReader:
    def read_assets(self, file_path):
        '''
        Reads NBA 2k26 asset files and extracts data.
        :param file_path: Path to the asset file.
        :return: Extracted data in dictionary format.
        '''
        try:
            with open(file_path, 'rb') as file:
                # Implement actual reading logic here
                # Example: Read binary data and parse it
                data = {}
                # Placeholder logic - needs actual implementation
                while chunk := file.read(8):
                    key, value = struct.unpack('4sI', chunk)
                    data[key.decode()] = value
                print(f"Successfully read assets from {file_path}")
                return data
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error reading assets: {e}")
            return None
    def export_to_json(self, data, output_path):
        '''
        Exports asset data to a JSON file.
        :param data: Data to be exported.
        :param output_path: Path to save the JSON file.
        '''
        try:
            with open(output_path, 'w') as json_file:
                json.dump(data, json_file, indent=4)
            print(f"Assets exported to JSON at {output_path}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error exporting to JSON: {e}")
    def export_to_dds(self, image_data, output_path):
        '''
        Exports image data to a DDS file.
        :param image_data: Image data to be exported.
        :param output_path: Path to save the DDS file.
        '''
        try:
            # Assuming image_data is a PIL Image object
            image_data.save(output_path, format='DDS')
            print(f"Assets exported to DDS at {output_path}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error exporting to DDS: {e}")
```

gui.py
```python
'''
Module for creating the graphical user interface for the NBA 2k26 asset tool.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import filedialog
from asset_reader import NBA2K26AssetReader
class GUI:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.asset_reader = NBA2K26AssetReader()
        self.create_main_window()
    def create_main_window(self):
        self.setup_buttons()
    def setup_buttons(self):
        import_button = tk.Button(self.master, text="Import Assets", command=self.on_import_click)
        import_button.pack()
        export_button = tk.Button(self.master, text="Export Assets", command=self.on_export_click)
        export_button.pack()
    def on_import_click(self):
        file_path = filedialog.askopenfilename(title="Select Asset File")
        if file_path:
            data = self.asset_reader.read_assets(file_path)
            print("Assets imported:", data)
    def on_export_click(self):
        output_path = filedialog.asksaveasfilename(title="Save JSON File", defaultextension=".json")
        if output_path:
            data = {"example": "data"}  # Replace with actual data
            self.asset_reader.export_to_json(data, output_path)
            print("Assets exported to JSON:", output_path)
```

blender_addon.py
```python
'''
Blender add-on for importing, editing, and exporting player models in JSON/DDS format.
'''
import bpy
import json
from bpy_extras.io_utils import ImportHelper, ExportHelper
class BlenderAddon:
    def import_model(self, json_file, dds_file):
        '''
        Imports player model from JSON and DDS files.
        :param json_file: Path to the JSON file containing model data.
        :param dds_file: Path to the DDS file containing texture data.
        '''
        try:
            with open(json_file, 'r') as file:
                model_data = json.load(file)
            # Load DDS texture
            texture = bpy.data.images.load(dds_file)
            # Create mesh and apply texture
            mesh = bpy.data.meshes.new(name="PlayerModel")
            obj = bpy.data.objects.new("PlayerModel", mesh)
            bpy.context.collection.objects.link(obj)
            obj.data.materials.append(bpy.data.materials.new(name="PlayerMaterial"))
            obj.data.materials[0].use_nodes = True
            bsdf = obj.data.materials[0].node_tree.nodes["Principled BSDF"]
            tex_image = obj.data.materials[0].node_tree.nodes.new('ShaderNodeTexImage')
            tex_image.image = texture
            obj.data.materials[0].node_tree.links.new(bsdf.inputs['Base Color'], tex_image.outputs['Color'])
            print(f"Model imported from {json_file} and {dds_file}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error importing model: {e}")
    def edit_model(self):
        '''
        Edits the player model.
        '''
        try:
            # Example: Apply a simple transformation
            for obj in bpy.context.selected_objects:
                obj.scale = (1.1, 1.1, 1.1)
            print("Model edited successfully.")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error editing model: {e}")
    def export_model(self, output_json, output_dds):
        '''
        Exports player model to JSON and DDS files.
        :param output_json: Path to save the JSON file.
        :param output_dds: Path to save the DDS file.
        '''
        try:
            # Export model data to JSON
            model_data = {"example": "model data"}  # Replace with actual model data
            with open(output_json, 'w') as json_file:
                json.dump(model_data, json_file, indent=4)
            # Export texture to DDS
            for obj in bpy.context.selected_objects:
                if obj.type == 'MESH' and obj.data.materials:
                    texture = obj.data.materials[0].node_tree.nodes['ShaderNodeTexImage'].image
                    texture.save_render(output_dds)
            print(f"Model exported to {output_json} and {output_dds}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error exporting model: {e}")
```

# LangChain

Building applications with LLMs through composability

Looking for the JS/TS version? Check out LangChain.js.

**Production Support:** As you move your LangChains into production, we'd love to offer more comprehensive support.

Please fill out this form and we'll set up a dedicated support Slack channel.

## Quick Install

`pip install langchain`

or

`conda install langchain -c conda-forge`

## 🤔 What is this?

Large language models (LLMs) are emerging as a transformative technology, enabling developers to build applications that they previously could not. However, using these LLMs in isolation is often insufficient for creating a truly powerful app - the real power comes when you can combine them with other sources of computation or knowledge.

This library aims to assist in the development of those types of applications. Common examples of these applications include:

**❓ Question Answering over specific documents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: Question Answering over Notion Database

**🤖 Agents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: GPT+WolframAlpha

- Getting started (installation, setting up the environment, simple examples)

- How-To examples (demos, integrations, helper functions)

- Reference (full API docs)

# NBA 2k26 Asset Tool User Manual

Welcome to the NBA 2k26 Asset Tool, a comprehensive software solution designed to read, export, and manipulate NBA 2k26 assets. This tool includes a standalone Windows application for asset management and a Blender 3.x add-on for model editing. Below is a detailed guide on how to install, use, and maximize the capabilities of this software.

## Main Functions

### Windows Standalone Tool

1. **Import Assets**: Read NBA 2k26 asset files and extract data.
2. **Export Assets**: Export extracted asset data to JSON and DDS formats.

### Blender 3.x Add-on

1. **Import Player Models**: Import player models using JSON and DDS files.
2. **Edit Player Models**: Modify player models, including transformations and texture adjustments.
3. **Export Player Models**: Save edited models back to JSON and DDS formats.

## Installation

### Prerequisites

Ensure you have the following software installed on your system:

- **Python 3.x**: Required for running the standalone tool and Blender add-on.
- **Blender 3.x**: Required for using the Blender add-on.

### Environment Setup

1. **Install Python Dependencies**:
   - Open your terminal or command prompt.
   - Run the following command to install necessary Python packages:
     ```bash
     pip install pillow tkinter
     ```

2. **Install Blender Add-on**:
   - Open Blender.
   - Navigate to `Edit` > `Preferences`.
   - In the `Add-ons` section, click `Install`.
   - Select the `blender_addon.py` file and enable the add-on.

## Usage

### Windows Standalone Tool

1. **Launch the Application**:
   - Run `main.py` using Python:
     ```bash
     python main.py
     ```
   - The GUI will open, titled "NBA 2k26 Asset Tool".

2. **Importing Assets**:
   - Click the "Import Assets" button.
   - Select the NBA 2k26 asset file you wish to import.
   - The tool will read and display the extracted data.

3. **Exporting Assets**:
   - Click the "Export Assets" button.
   - Choose a location to save the JSON file.
   - The tool will export the data to the specified location.

### Blender 3.x Add-on

1. **Importing Player Models**:
   - Open Blender and ensure the add-on is enabled.
   - Use the add-on interface to select and import JSON and DDS files.
   - The player model will be loaded into Blender.

2. **Editing Player Models**:
   - Select the model in Blender.
   - Apply transformations or texture modifications as needed.
   - Use Blender's editing tools to refine the model.

3. **Exporting Player Models**:
   - Use the add-on interface to export the model.
   - Choose locations to save the JSON and DDS files.
   - The edited model will be saved in the specified formats.

## Support and Documentation

For further assistance and detailed documentation, please refer to our [online resources](https://chatdev.com/nba2k26-tool-docs). If you encounter any issues or have questions, feel free to contact our support team.

Thank you for choosing the NBA 2k26 Asset Tool. We hope it enhances your asset management and model editing experience.
